adds works to linked_docs, recording their edition key and index in docs_dict if present.\n   264→        for doc in solr_docs:\n   265→            if doc[\"key\"].startswith(\"/works\"):\n   266→                linked_docs.append(doc)\n   267→                if doc.get(\"logged_edition\"):\n   268→                    editions_to_work_doc.update({doc[\"logged_edition\"]: doc})\n   269→        # Attaches editions to the works, in second loop-- in case of misperformed order.\n   270→        for edition in solr_docs:\n   271→            if edition[\"key\"].startswith(\"/books/\"):\n   272→                if work_doc := editions_to_work_doc.get(edition[\"key\"]):\n   273→                    work_doc.editions = [edition]\n   274→                else:\n   275→                    # Because\n   288→        we use Solr to build the lists of storage items that ultimately gets passed\n   289→        to the templates, redirected items returned from the reading log DB will\n   290→        'disappear' when not returned by Solr. This remedies that by filling in\n   291→        dummy works, albeit with the correct work_id.\n   292→        \"\"\"\n   293→\n   294→        from openlibrary.plugins.worksearch.code import run_solr_query\n   295→\n   296→        fetched_keys = {doc[\"key\"] for doc in solr_docs}\n   297→        missing_keys = {work for (work, _) in reading_log_keys} - fetched_keys\n   298→\n   299→        \"\"\"\n   300→        Provides a proper 1-to-1 connection between work keys and edition keys; needed, in order to fill in the appropriate 'logged_edition' data\n   301→        for the correctly pulled work later on, as well as to correctly update the post-redirect version back to the pre_redirect key.\n   302→        Without this step, processes may error due to the 'post-redirect key' not actually existing within a user's reading log.\n   303→        \"\"\"\n   304→        work_to_edition_keys = {\n   305→            work: edition for (work, edition) in reading_log_keys if edition\n   306→        }\n   307→        edition_to_work_keys = {\n   308→            edition: work for (work, edition) in reading_log_keys if edition\n   309→        }\n   310→\n   311→        # Here, we add in dummied works for situations in which there is no edition key present, yet the work key accesses a redirect.\n   312→        # Ideally, this will be rare, as there's no way to access the relevant information through Solr.\n   313→        for key in missing_keys.copy():\n   314→            if not work_to_edition_keys.get(key):\n   315→                missing_keys.remove(key)\n   316→                solr_docs.append(web.storage({\"key\": key}))\n   317→\n   318→        edition_keys_to_query = [\n   319→            work_to_edition_keys[key].split(\"/\")[2] for key in missing_keys\n   320→        ]\n   321→        fq = f'edition_key:({\" OR \".join(edition_keys_to_query)})'\n   322→        if not edition_keys_to_query:\n   323→            return\n   324→\n   325→        solr_resp = run_solr_query(\n   326→            scheme=WorkSearchScheme(),\n   327→            param={'q': '*:*'},\n   328→            rows=len(edition_keys_to_query),\n   329→            fields=list(\n   330→                WorkSearchScheme.default_fetched_fields\n   331→                | {'subject', 'person', 'place', 'time', 'edition_key'}\n   332→            ),\n   333→            facet=False,\n   334→            extra_params=[(\"fq\", fq)],\n   335→        )\n   336→\n   337→        \"\"\"\n   338→        Now, we add the correct 'logged_edition' information to each document retrieved by the query, and substitute the work_key in\n   339→        each doc for the original one.\n   340→        \"\"\"\n   341→        for doc in solr_resp.docs:\n   342→            for edition_key in doc[\"edition_key\"]:\n   343→                if pre_redirect_key := edition_to_work_keys.get(\n   344→                    '/books/%s' % edition_key\n   345→                ):\n   346→                    doc[\"key\"] = pre_redirect_key\n   347→                    doc[\"logged_edition\"] = work_to_edition_keys.get(pre_redirect_key)\n   348→                    solr_docs.append(web.storage(doc))\n   349→                    break\n   350→\n   351→    @classmethod\n   352→    def add_storage_items_for_deletes(\n   353→        cls, reading_log_keys, solr_docs: list[web.Storage]\n   354→    ):\n   355→        missing = {w for w, e in reading_log_keys} - {doc['key'] for doc in solr_docs}\n   356→        # Get them from the DB\n   357→        missing_docs = web.ctx.site.get_many(list(missing))\n            web.storage(\n   364→                        {\n   365→                            'key': doc.key,\n   366→                            'title': _('[Record deleted]'),\n   367→                        }\n   368→                    )\n   369→                )\n   370→            else:\n   371→                # Should never happen?\n   372→                logger.warning(f\"Missing item in get_users_logged_books(\n   384→        cls,\n   385→        username: str,\n   386→        bookshelf_id: int = 0,\n   387→        limit: int = 100,\n   388→        page: int = 1,  # Not zero-based 1),\n   417→            'bookshelf_id': bookshelf_id,\n   418→            'checkin_year': checkin_year,\n   419→        }\n   420→\n   421→        @dataclass\n   422→        class ReadingLogItem:\n   423→            \"\"\"Holds the datetime a book was logged and the edition ID.\"\"\"\n   424→\n   425→            logged_date: datetime\n   426→            edition_id: str\n   427→\n   428→        def add_reading_log_data(\n   429→            reading_log_books: list[web.storage], solr_docs: list[web.storage]\n   430→        ):\n   431→            \"\"\"\n   432→            Adds data from ReadingLogItem to the Solr responses so they have the logged\n   433→            date and edition ID.\n   434→            \"\"\"\n   435→            # Create a mapping of work keys to ReadingLogItem from the reading log DB.\n   436→            reading_log_store: dict[str, ReadingLogItem] = {\n   437→                f\"/works/OL{book.work_id}W\": ReadingLogItem(\n   438→                    logged_date=book.created,\n   439→                    edition_id=(\n   440→                        f\"/books/OL{book.edition_id}M\"\n   441→                        if book.edition_id is not None\n   442→                        else \"\"\n   443→                    ),\n   444→                )\n   445→                for book in reading_log_books\n   446→            }\n   447→\n   448→            # Insert {logged_edition} if present and {logged_date} into the Solr work.\n   449→            # These dates are not used for sort-by-added-date. The DB handles that.\n   450→            # Currently only used in JSON requests.\n   451→            for doc in solr_docs:\n   452→                if reading_log_record := reading_log_store.get(doc.key):\n   453→                    doc.logged_date = reading_log_record.logged_date\n   454→                    doc.logged_edition = reading_log_record.edition_id\n   455→\n   456→            return solr_docs\n   457→\n   458→        def get_filtered_reading_log_books(\n   459→            q: str,\n   460→            query_params: dict[str, str | int | None],\n   461→            filter_book_limit: int,\n   462→            fq: list[str] | None = None,\n   463→        ) -> LoggedBooksData:\n   464→            \"\"\"\n   465→            Filter reading log books based an a query and return LoggedBooksData.\n   466→            This does not work with sorting.\n   467→\n   468→            The reading log DB alone has access to who logged which book to their\n   469→            reading log, so we need to get work IDs and logged info from there, query\n   470→            Solr for more complete book information, and then put the logged info into\n   471→            the Solr response.\n   472→            \"\"\"\n   473→            # Filtering by query needs a larger limit as we need (ideally) all of a\n   474→            # user's added works from the reading log DB. The logged work IDs are used\n   475→            # to query Solr, which searches for matches related to those work IDs.\n   476→            query_params[\"limit\"] = filter_book_limit\n   477→\n   478→            query = (\n   479→                \"SELECT work_id, created, edition_id from bookshelves_books WHERE \"\n   480→                \"bookshelf_id=$bookshelf_id AND username=$username \"\n   481→                \"LIMIT $limit\"\n   482→            )\n   483→\n   484→            reading_log_books: list[web.storage] = list(\n   485→                oldb.query(query, vars=query_params)\n   486→            )\n   487→\n   488→            assert len(reading_log_books) <= filter_book_limit\n   489→\n   490→            work_to_edition_keys = {\n   491→                '/works/OL%sW' % i['work_id']: '/books/OL%sM' % i['edition_id']\n   492→                for i in reading_log_books\n   493→            }\n   494→\n   495→            # Separating out the filter query from the call allows us to cleanly edit it, if editions are required.\n   496→            filter_query = 'key:(%s)' % \" OR \".join(\n   497→                '\"%s\"' % key for key in work_to_edition_keys\n   498→            )\n   499→\n   500→            solr_resp = run_solr_query(\n   501→                scheme=WorkSearchScheme(),\n   502→                param={'q': q or '*:*'},\n   503→                offset=query_params[\"offset\"],\n   504→                rows=limit,\n   505→                facet=False,\n   506→                extra_params=[\n   507→                    # Putting these in fq allows them to avoid user-query processing, which\n   508→                    # can be (surprisingly) slow if we have ~20k OR clauses.\n   509→                    ('fq', filter_query),\n   510→                    *[('fq', f) for f in (fq or [])],\n   511→                ],\n   512→            )\n   513→            total_results = solr_resp.num_found\n   514→            solr_docs = solr_resp.docs\n   515→            edition_data = get_solr().get_many(\n   516→                [work_to_edition_keys[work[\"key\"]] for work in solr_resp.docs],\n   517→                fields=WorkSearchScheme.default_fetched_fields\n   518→                | {'subject', 'person', 'place', 'time', 'edition_key'},\n   519→            )\n   520→\n   521→            solr_docs.extend(edition_data)\n   522→\n   523→            # Downstream many things expect a list of web.storage docs.\n   524→            solr_docs = [web.storage(doc) for doc in solr_resp.docs]\n   525→            solr_docs = add_reading_log_data(reading_log_books, solr_docs)\n   526→            solr_docs = cls.link_editions_to_works(solr_docs)\n   527→\n   528→            return LoggedBooksData(\n   529→                username=username,\n   530→                q=q,\n   531→                page_size=limit,\n   532→                total_results=total_results,\n   533→                shelf_totals=shelf_totals,\n   534→                docs=solr_docs,\n   535→            )\n   536→\n   537→        def get_sorted_reading_log_books(\n   538→            query_params: dict[str, str | int | None],\n   539→            sort: Literal['created asc', 'created desc'],\n   540→            checkin_year: int | None,\n   541→        ):\n   542→            \"\"\"\n   543→            Get a page of sorted books from the reading log. Because\n        we use Solr to build the lists of storage items that ultimately gets passed\n        to the templates, redirected items returned from the reading log DB will\n        'disappear' when not returned by Solr. This remedies that by filling in\n        dummy works, albeit with the correct work_id.\n        \"\"\"\n\n        from openlibrary.plugins.worksearch.code import run_solr_query\n\n        fetched_keys = {doc[\"key\"] for doc in solr_docs}\n        missing_keys = {work for (work, _) in reading_log_keys} - fetched_keys\n\n        \"\"\"\n        Provides a proper 1-to-1 connection between work keys and edition keys; needed, in order to fill in the appropriate 'logged_edition' data\n        for the correctly pulled work later on, as well as to correctly update the post-redirect version back to the pre_redirect key.\n        Without this step, processes may error due to the 'post-redirect key' not actually existing within a user's reading log.\n        \"\"\"\n        work_to_edition_keys = {\n            work: edition for (work, edition) in reading_log_keys if edition\n        }\n        edition_to_work_keys = {\n            edition: work for (work, edition) in reading_log_keys if edition\n        }\n\n        # Here, we add in dummied works for situations in which there is no edition key present, yet the work key accesses a redirect.\n        # Ideally, this will be rare, as there's no way to access the relevant information through Solr.\n        for key in missing_keys.copy():\n            if not work_to_edition_keys.get(key):\n                missing_keys.remove(key)\n                solr_docs.append(web.storage({\"key\": key}))\n\n        edition_keys_to_query = [\n            work_to_edition_keys[key].split(\"/\")[2] for key in missing_keys\n        ]\n        fq = f'edition_key:({\" OR \".join(edition_keys_to_query)})'\n        if not edition_keys_to_query:\n            return\n\n        solr_resp = run_solr_query(\n            scheme=WorkSearchScheme(),\n            param={'q': '*:*'},\n            rows=len(edition_keys_to_query),\n            fields=list(\n                WorkSearchScheme.default_fetched_fields\n                | {'subject', 'person', 'place', 'time', 'edition_key'}\n            ),\n            facet=False,\n            extra_params=[(\"fq\", fq)],\n        )\n\n        \"\"\"\n        Now, we add the correct 'logged_edition' information to each document retrieved by the query, and substitute the work_key in\n        each doc for the original one.\n        \"\"\"\n        for doc in solr_resp.docs:\n            for edition_key in doc[\"edition_key\"]:\n                if pre_redirect_key := edition_to_work_keys.get(\n                    '/books/%s' % edition_key\n                ):\n                    doc[\"key\"] = pre_redirect_key\n                    doc[\"logged_edition\"] = work_to_edition_keys.get(pre_redirect_key)\n                    solr_docs.append(web.storage(doc))\n                    break\n\n    @classmethod\n    def add_storage_items_for_deletes(\n        cls, reading_log_keys, solr_docs: list[web.Storage]\n    ):\n        missing = {w for w, e in reading_log_keys} - {doc['key'] for doc in solr_docs}\n        # Get them from the DB\n        missing_docs = web.ctx.site.get_many(list(missing))\n\n        # Push some dummy books\n        for doc in missing_docs:\n            if doc.type.key == '/type/delete':\n                solr_docs.append(\n                    web.storage(\n                        {\n                            'key': doc.key,\n                            'title': _('[Record deleted]'),\n                        }\n                    )\n                )\n            else:\n                # Should never happen?\n                logger.warning(f\"Missing item in Solr: {doc.key}\")\n                solr_docs.append(\n                    web.storage(\n                        {\n                            'key': doc.key,\n                            'title': doc.key,\n                        }\n                    )\n                )\n\n    @classmethod\n    def get_users_logged_books(\n        cls,\n        username: str,\n        bookshelf_id: int = 0,\n        limit: int = 100,\n        page: int = 1,  # Not zero-based counting!\n        sort: Literal['created asc', 'created desc'] = 'created desc',\n        checkin_year: int | None = None,\n        q: str = \"\",\n        fq: list[str] | None = None,\n    ) -> Any:  # Circular imports prevent type hinting LoggedBooksData\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns LoggedBooksData containing Reading Log database records for books that\n        the user has logged. Also allows filtering/searching the reading log shelves,\n        and sorting reading log shelves (when not filtering).\n\n        The returned records ultimately come from Solr so that, as much as possible,\n        these query results may be used by anything relying on logged book data.\n\n        :param username: who logged this book\n        :param bookshelf_id: the ID of the bookshelf, see: PRESET_BOOKSHELVES.\n            If bookshelf_id is None, return books from all bookshelves.\n        :param q: an optional query string to filter the results.\n        \"\"\"\n        from openlibrary.core.models import LoggedBooksData\n        from openlibrary.plugins.worksearch.code import run_solr_query\n\n        shelf_totals = cls.count_total_books_logged_by_user_per_shelf(username)\n        oldb = db.get_db()\n        page = int(page or 1)\n        query_params: dict[str, str | int | None] = {\n            'username': username,\n            'limit': limit,\n            'offset': limit * (page - 1),\n            'bookshelf_id': bookshelf_id,\n            'checkin_year': checkin_year,\n        }\n\n        @dataclass\n        class ReadingLogItem:\n            \"\"\"Holds the datetime a book was logged and the edition ID.\"\"\"\n\n            logged_date: datetime\n            edition_id: str\n\n        def add_reading_log_data(\n            reading_log_books: list[web.storage], solr_docs: list[web.storage]\n        ):\n            \"\"\"\n            Adds data from ReadingLogItem to the Solr responses so they have the logged\n            date and edition ID.\n            \"\"\"\n            # Create a mapping of work keys to ReadingLogItem from the reading log DB.\n            reading_log_store: dict[str, ReadingLogItem] = {\n                f\"/works/OL{book.work_id}W\": ReadingLogItem(\n                    logged_date=book.created,\n                    edition_id=(\n                        f\"/books/OL{book.edition_id}M\"\n                        if book.edition_id is not None\n                        else \"\"\n                    ),\n                )\n                for book in reading_log_books\n            }\n\n            # Insert {logged_edition} if present and {logged_date} into the Solr work.\n            # These dates are not used for sort-by-added-date. The DB handles that.\n            # Currently only used in JSON requests.\n            for doc in solr_docs:\n                if reading_log_record := reading_log_store.get(doc.key):\n                    doc.logged_date = reading_log_record.logged_date\n                    doc.logged_edition = reading_log_record.edition_id\n\n            return solr_docs\n\n        def get_filtered_reading_log_books(\n            q: str,\n            query_params: dict[str, str | int | None],\n            filter_book_limit: int,\n            fq: list[str] | None = None,\n        ) -> LoggedBooksData:\n            \"\"\"\n            Filter reading log books based an a query and return LoggedBooksData.\n            This does not work with sorting.\n\n            The reading log DB alone has access to who logged which book to their\n            reading log, so we need to get work IDs and logged info from there, query\n            Solr for more complete book information, and then put the logged info into\n            the Solr response.\n            \"\"\"\n            # Filtering by query needs a larger limit as we need (ideally) all of a\n            # user's added works from the reading log DB. The logged work IDs are used\n            # to query Solr, which searches for matches related to those work IDs.\n            query_params[\"limit\"] = filter_book_limit\n\n            query = (\n                \"SELECT work_id, created, edition_id from bookshelves_books WHERE \"\n                \"bookshelf_id=$bookshelf_id AND username=$username \"\n                \"LIMIT $limit\"\n            )\n\n            reading_log_books: list[web.storage] = list(\n                oldb.query(query, vars=query_params)\n            )\n\n            assert len(reading_log_books) <= filter_book_limit\n\n            work_to_edition_keys = {\n                '/works/OL%sW' % i['work_id']: '/books/OL%sM' % i['edition_id']\n                for i in reading_log_books\n            }\n\n            # Putting these in fq allows them to avoid user-query processing, which\n                    # can be (surprisingly) slow if we have ~20k OR clauses.\n                    ('fq', filter_query),\n                    *[('fq', f) for f in (fq or [])],\n                ],\n            )\n            total_results = solr_resp.num_found\n            solr_docs = solr_resp.docs\n            edition_data = get_solr().get_many(\n                [work_to_edition_keys[work[\"key\"]] for work in solr_resp.docs],\n                fields=WorkSearchScheme.default_fetched_fields\n                | {'subject', 'person', 'place', 'time', 'edition_key'},\n            )\n\n            solr_docs.extend(edition_data)\n\n            # Downstream many things expect a list of web.storage docs.\n            solr_docs = [web.storage(doc) for doc in solr_resp.docs]\n            solr_docs = add_reading_log_data(reading_log_books, solr_docs)\n            solr_docs = cls.link_editions_to_works(solr_docs)\n\n            return LoggedBooksData(\n                username=username,\n                q=q,\n                page_size=limit,\n                total_results=total_results,\n                shelf_totals=shelf_totals,\n                docs=solr_docs,\n            )\n\n        def get_sorted_reading_log_books(\n            query_params: dict[str, str | int | None],\n            sort: Literal['created asc', 'created desc'],\n            checkin_year: int | None,\n        ):\n            \"\"\"\n            Get a page of sorted books from the reading log. This does not work with\n            filtering/searching the reading log.\n\n            The reading log DB alone has access to who logged which book to their\n            reading log, so we need to get work IDs and logged info from there, query\n            Solr for more complete book information, and then put the logged info into\n            the Solr response.\n            \"\"\"\n            if checkin_year:\n                query = \"\"\"\n                SELECT b.work_id, b.created, b.edition_id\n                FROM bookshelves_books b\n                INNER JOIN bookshelves_events e\n                ON b.work_id = e.work_id AND b.username = e.username\n                WHERE b.username = $username\n                AND e.event_date LIKE $checkin_year || '%'\n                ORDER BY b.created DESC\n                \"\"\"\n            else:\n                query = (\n                    \"SELECT work_id, created, edition_id from bookshelves_books WHERE \"\n                    \"bookshelf_id=$bookshelf_id AND username=$username \"\n                    f\"ORDER BY created {'DESC' if sort == 'created desc' else 'ASC'} \"\n                    \"LIMIT $limit OFFSET $offset\"\n                )\n\n            if not bookshelf_id:\n                query = \"SELECT * from bookshelves_books WHERE username=$username\"\n                # XXX Removing limit, offset, etc from data looks like a bug\n                # unrelated / not fixing in this PR.\n                query_params = {'username': username}\n            reading_log_books: list[web.storage] = list(\n                oldb.query(query, vars=query_params)\n            )\n\n            reading_log_keys = [\n                (\n                    ['/works/OL%sW' % i['work_id'], '/books/OL%sM' % i['edition_id']]\n                    if i['edition_id']\n                    else ['/works/OL%sW' % i['work_id'], \"\"]\n                )\n                for i in reading_log_books\n            ]\n\n            solr_docs = get_solr().get_many(\n                [key for key in flatten(reading_log_keys) if key],\n                fields=WorkSearchScheme.default_fetched_fields\n                | {'subject', 'person', 'place', 'time', 'edition_key'},\n            )\n\n            cls.add_storage_items_for_redirects(reading_log_keys, solr_docs)\n            if len(solr_docs) < len(reading_log_keys):\n                cls.add_storage_items_for_deletes(reading_log_keys, solr_docs)\n\n            total_results = shelf_totals.get(bookshelf_id, 0)\n            solr_docs = add_reading_log_data(reading_log_books, solr_docs)\n            solr_docs = cls.link_editions_to_works(solr_docs)\n\n            return LoggedBooksData(\n                username=username,\n                q=q,\n                page_size=limit,\n                total_results=total_results,\n                shelf_totals=shelf_totals,\n                docs=solr_docs,\n            )\n\n        if q or fq:\n            # So, instead of creating a big list, let's repeatedly\n        get small lists like get_users_logged_books() and yield one book at a time.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not username or not isinstance(username, str):\n            raise ValueError(f\"username must be a string, not {username}.\")\n        oldb = db.get_db()\n        block = 0\n        LIMIT = 100  # Is there an ideal block size?!?\n\n        def get_a_block_of_books() -> list:\n            data = {\"username\": username, \"limit\": LIMIT, \"offset\": LIMIT * block}\n            query = (\n                \"SELECT * from bookshelves_books WHERE username=$username \"\n                \"ORDER BY created DESC LIMIT $limit OFFSET $offset\"\n            )\n            return list(oldb.query(query, vars=data))\n\n        while books := get_a_block_of_books():\n            block += 1\n            yield from books\n\n    @classmethod\n    def get_recently_logged_books(\n        cls,\n        bookshelf_id: str | None = None,\n        limit: int = 50,\n        page: int = 1,\n    ) -> list:\n        oldb = db.get_db()\n        page = int(page or 1)\n        data = {\n            'bookshelf_id': bookshelf_id,\n            'limit': limit,\n            'offset': limit * (page - 1),\n        }\n        where = \"WHERE bookshelf_id=$bookshelf_id \" if bookshelf_id else \"\"\n        query = (\n            f\"SELECT * from bookshelves_books {where} \"\n            \"ORDER BY created DESC LIMIT $limit OFFSET $offset\"\n        )\n        return list(oldb.query(query, vars=data))\n\n    @classmethod\n    def get_users_read_status_of_work(cls, username: str, work_id: str) -> int | None:\n        \"\"\"A user can mark a book as (1) want to read, (2) currently reading,\n        or (3) already read. If that is what you want, add all server names to\n        this service to make things explicit.\n        \"\"\"\n        with open(p(\"..\", \"compose.production.yaml\")) as f:\n            prod_dc: dict = yaml.safe_load(f)\n        for serv, opts in prod_dc[\"services\"].items():\n            assert \"profiles\" in opts, f\"{serv} is missing 'profiles' field\"\n\n    def test_shared_constants(self):\n        # read the value in compose.yaml\n        with open(p(\"..\", \"compose.yaml\")) as f:\n            prod_dc: dict = yaml.safe_load(f)\n        solr_service = prod_dc[\"services\"][\"solr\"]\n        solr_opts = next(var.split(\"=\", 1)[1] for var in solr_service[\"environment\"] if var.startswith(\"SOLR_OPTS=\"))\n        solr_opts_max_boolean_clauses = next(int(opt.split(\"=\", 1)[1]) for opt in solr_opts.split() if opt.startswith(\"-Dsolr.max.booleanClauses\"))\n\n        # read the value in openlibrary/core/bookshelves.py\n        from openlibrary.core.bookshelves import FILTER_BOOK_LIMIT\n\n        assert solr_opts_max_boolean_clauses >= FILTER_BOOK_LIMIT\n","numLines":50,"startLine":1,"totalLines":50}}}
